<p><b>Gwalior</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Gwalior.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/Gwalior.ogg" title="Gwalior.ogg">pronunciatio</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Gwalior.ogg" title="File:Gwalior.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) is a major city in the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and one of the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)#Counter_magnets" title="National Capital Region (India)">Counter-magnet</a> cities. Located 319 kilometres (198 mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, the capital city of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, Gwalior occupies a strategic location in the <a href="/wiki/Gird" title="Gird">Gird</a> region of India. The city and its fortress have been ruled by several historic northern Indian kingdoms. From the <a href="/wiki/Tomar_clan" title="Tomar clan">Tomars</a> in the 13th century, it was passed on to the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, then to the <a href="/wiki/Maratha" title="Maratha">Maratha</a> in 1754, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Scindia" title="Scindia">Scindia</a> in 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet.com_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet.com-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides being the administrative headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_district" title="Gwalior district">Gwalior district</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_division" title="Gwalior division">Gwalior division</a>, Gwalior has many administrative offices of the <a href="/wiki/Chambal_division" title="Chambal division">Chambal division</a> of northern Madhya Pradesh. Several administrative and judicial organisations, commissions and boards have their state and national headquarters situated in the city.</p>
<p>Gwalior was the winter capital of the state of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Bharat" title="Madhya Bharat">Madhya Bharat</a> which later became a part of the larger state of Madhya Pradesh. Prior to <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence</a> on 15 August 1947, Gwalior remained a princely state of the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a> with the Scindia as the local rulers. High rocky hills surround the city from all sides, on the north it just forms the border of the Ganga- Yamuna Drainage Basin. The city however is situated in the valley between the hills. Gwalior's metropolitan area includes <a href="/wiki/Lashkar_Gwalior" title="Lashkar Gwalior">Lashkar Gwalior</a> (Lashkar Subcity), <a href="/wiki/Morar,_Gwalior_district" title="Morar, Gwalior district">Morar Gwalior</a> (Morar Subcity), <a href="/wiki/Thatipur" title="Thatipur">Thatipur</a>, and the city centre.</p>
<p>Gwalior was one of the major sites of rebellion during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1857_uprising" title="1857 uprising">1857 uprising</a>. Post-independence, Gwalior has emerged as an important tourist attraction in central India while many industries and administrative offices came up within the city. Before the end of the 20th century it became a million plus agglomeration and now it is a metropolitan city in central India. Gwalior is surrounded by industrial and commercial zones of neighbouring districts (Malanpur – <a href="/wiki/Bhind" title="Bhind">Bhind</a>, Banmor – <a href="/wiki/Morena" title="Morena">Morena</a>) on all three main directions. A 2016 report of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> found Gwalior to be the second-most air-polluted city in the world and the most polluted city in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gwalior has been selected as one of the hundred Indian cities to be developed as a <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a> under <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">PM Narendra Modi's</a> flagship <a href="/wiki/Smart_Cities_Mission" title="Smart Cities Mission">Smart Cities Mission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to local tradition, Gwalior owes its name to a sage of former times. Suraj Sen, a prince of the <i>gurjar-pratihar</i> clan of the eighth century, is said to have lost his way in the forest. On a secluded hill, he met an old man, the sage Gwalipa, whose influence almost took him by surprise. Upon asking the sage for some drinking water, he was led to a pond, where the waters not only quenched his thirst but cured him of <a href="/wiki/Leprosy" title="Leprosy">leprosy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet.com_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet.com-3">[3]</a></sup> Out of gratitude, the prince wished to offer the sage something in return, and the sage asked him to build a wall on the hill to protect the other sages from wild animals which often disturbed their <i><a href="/wiki/Yajna" title="Yajna">yajnas</a></i> (or <i>pujas</i>). Suraj Sen later built a palace inside the fort, which was named "Gwalior" after the sage, and eventually the city that grew around the fort took the same name.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="409" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg/220px-The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg/330px-The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Maharahaj_of_Gwalior_Before_His_Palace_ca_1887.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Maharahaj of Gwalior Before His Palace c. 1887</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After being founded by Maharaj Suraj Sen, Gwalior Fort saw many different rulers ruling the city and suburbs around it. Gwalior became a prominent place for religious practices, cultures and other disciplines coming up during that time in the country. During the 6th century BC Gwalior was ruled by the Nanda dynasty of Pataliputra. During the first century AD, Gwalior came under Naga Dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> From the carving found at Pawaya, it has been discovered that the kushanas ruled the city till the 3rd century AD. After that, it came under the Guptas till 467 AD. During the 5th century, The Kannauj of Gurar-Pratihara Dynasty ruled Gwalior and played a prominent role in shaping its history. From 700–740 AD Gwalior (fondly called then as Gopal Giri) became the capital of Kannauj. A Magnificent Sun Temple was created at the fort hill during that period.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jain_statues,_Gwalior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2585" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg/220px-Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg/330px-Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg/440px-Jain_statues%2C_Gwalior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jain_statues,_Gwalior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jain statues at Gwalior built by dungar singh</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Later Kachwaha became the rulers of Gwalior. The Padavali Group of Monuments near Morena, Sahastrabahu Temple at the Fort, Kankadmad, were built under their rule.</p>
<p>During 1195–96 <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_of_Ghor" title="Muhammad of Ghor">Muhammad of Ghor</a> (also called Muhammad Ghori) invaded Gwalior and planned a mass destruction to capture the fort. But he failed as the fort was unconquerable under the brave efforts of Parihars. In 1231 <a href="/wiki/Iltutmish" title="Iltutmish">Iltutmish</a> captured Gwalior after an 11-month-long effort and from then till the 13th century it remained under Muslim Rule. In 1375, Raja Veer Singh was made the ruler of Gwalior and he founded the rule of the Tomars in Gwalior. During those years, Gwalior saw its golden period.</p>
<p>The Jain Sculptures at Gwalior Fort were built during Tomar's rule. Raja Man Singh made his dream palace, the Maan Mandir Palace which is now a centre of tourist attraction at Gwalior Fort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madan_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Madan-7">[7]</a></sup> Babur described it as "the pearl in the necklace of forts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Hind" title="Al-Hind">India</a> and not even the winds could touch its masts". The daily Light and Sound Show organised there tells about the history of the Gwalior Fort and Man Mandir Palace. Later in the 1730s, the <a href="/wiki/Scindia" title="Scindia">Scindias</a> captured Gwalior and it remained a princely state during the British Rule.</p>
<p>Ganesh temple at Gwalior Fort has the very first occurrence of zero as a written number in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> By the 15th century, the city had a noted singing school which was attended by <a href="/wiki/Tansen" title="Tansen">Tansen</a>. Gwalior was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Maratha" title="Maratha">Marathas</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2739" data-file-width="2630" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg/220px-Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg/330px-Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg/440px-Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gorgeous_Gwalior_Fort.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Maan Mandir Palace at Gwalior Fort</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebellion_of_1857">Rebellion of 1857</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rebellion of 1857">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior is also known for not participating in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">1857 rebellion</a>, mainly due to non-co-operation with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rani_Lakshmibai" title="Rani Lakshmibai">Rani Lakshmibai</a>. After Kalpi (Jhansi) fell into the hands of the British on 24<span class="nowrap"> </span>May 1858, Lakshmibai sought shelter at Gwalior Fort. The Maharaja of Gwalior was not willing to give up his fort without a fight as he was a strong ally of the British, but after negotiations, his troops capitulated and the rebels took possession of the fort. The British attacked Gwalior in no time, the battle was fought by Lakshmibai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Indian forces numbered around 20,000, and British forces around 1600 assisted by Maharaja of Gwalior troops. Lakshmibai's example is remembered to this day by Indian nationalists. She died fighting, and Gwalior was free from rebels. There is a statue of Lakshmibai on her horse which commemorates her contribution to the fight for independence. <a href="/wiki/Tatya_Tope" title="Tatya Tope">Tatya Tope</a> and Rao Sahib escaped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Tatya Tope was later captured and hanged in April 1859.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Princely_state_of_Gwalior">Princely state of Gwalior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Princely state of Gwalior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Scindia" title="Scindia">Scindia</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Maratha" title="Maratha">Maratha</a> clan in India. This clan included rulers of the <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_State" title="Gwalior State">Gwalior State</a> in the 18th and 19th centuries, collaborators of the colonial British government during the 19th and the 20th centuries until India became independent, and politicians in independent India.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_State" title="Gwalior State">Scindia state</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> of Gwalior became a major regional power in the second half of the 18th century and figured prominently in the three <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Maratha_Wars" title="Anglo-Maratha Wars">Anglo-Maratha Wars</a>. (Gwalior first fell to the British in 1780.) The Scindias held significant power over many of the <a href="/wiki/Rajput" title="Rajput">Rajput</a> states, and conquered the state of Ajmer. During the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">Indian Rebellion of 1857</a>, the city was briefly held by rebel forces in 1858 until they were defeated by the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The Scindia family ruled Gwalior until India's independence from the United Kingdom in 1947, when the <a href="/wiki/Maharaja" title="Maharaja">Maharaja</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jivajirao_Scindia" title="Jivajirao Scindia">Jivajirao Scindia</a> acceded to the Government of India. Gwalior was merged with a number of other princely states to become the new Indian state of Madhya Bharat. Jivajirao Scindia served as the state's <a href="/wiki/Rajpramukh" title="Rajpramukh">Rajpramukh</a>, or the appointed governor, from 28 May 1948 to 31 October 1956, when Madhya Bharat was merged into Madhya Pradesh.</p>
<p>In 1962, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajmata_Vijayraje_Scindia" title="Rajmata Vijayraje Scindia">Rajmata Vijayraje Scindia</a>, the widow of Maharaja Jivajirao Scindia, was elected to the Lok Sabha, beginning the family's career in electoral politics. She was first a member of the Congress Party, and later became an influential member of the Bharatiya Janata Party. Her son, Maharaja <a href="/wiki/Madhavrao_Scindia" title="Madhavrao Scindia">Madhavrao Scindia</a> was elected to the Lok Sabha in 1971 representing the Congress Party, and served until his death in 2001. His son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jyotiraditya_Scindia" title="Jyotiraditya Scindia">Jyotiraditya Scindia</a>, also in the Congress Party, was elected to the seat formerly held by his father in 2004.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Madhya_Pradesh" title="List of cities in Madhya Pradesh">List of cities in Madhya Pradesh</a></div>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>'s India census,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Gwalior has a population of 19,53,505. Males constitute 53% of the population and females 47%. Gwalior has an average literacy rate of 87.20%, higher than the national average of 74%: male literacy is 90.85%, and female literacy is 78.82%. In Gwalior, 13% of the population is under 6 years of age.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hinduism is practised by the majority of the people in Gwalior (88.84%). Other religions practised include Islam (8.58%), Jainism (1.41%), Sikhism (0.56%) and Christianity (0.29).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> in its standard form is widely spoken in Gwalior. <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a> is the second biggest language of the city, spoken by 20% of the population. There is a strong <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a> influence in Gwalior due to Maratha Rule over the centuries.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Gwalior is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Gwalior&amp;params=26.22_N_78.18_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">26°13′N</span> <span class="longitude">78°11′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">26.22°N 78.18°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">26.22; 78.18</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> in northern Madhya Pradesh 300 km (186 miles) from Delhi. It has an average elevation of 197 metres (646 feet). Most part of it comes under Bundelkhand area.</p>

<td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in °F</td>

<td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td>

</td>

</table>
<p>Gwalior has a sub-tropical climate with hot summers from late March to early July, the humid monsoon season from late June to early October, and a cool dry winter from early November to late February. Under <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen's climate classification</a> the city has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>. The highest recorded temperature was 48 °C and the lowest was −1 °C. Summers start in late March, and along with other cities like <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Delhi" title="Climate of Delhi">Delhi</a>, are among the hottest in India and the world. Temperatures peak in May and June with daily averages being around 33–35 °C (93–95 °F), and end in late June with the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>. Gwalior receives 900 mm (35 in) of rain on average per year, most of which is concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">Monsoon</a> months (from late June to early October). August is the wettest month with about 310 mm (12 in) of rain. Winter in Gwalior starts in late October, and is generally very mild with daily temperatures averaging in the 14–16 °C (58–62 °F) range, and mostly dry and sunny conditions. January is the coldest month with average lows in the 0 °C range (32 °F) and occasional cold snaps that plummet temperatures down to zero.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_Institutions">Government and Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_Municipal_Corporation" title="Gwalior Municipal Corporation">Gwalior Municipal Corporation</a></div>
<p>Gwalior Municipal Corporation is responsible for the civic infrastructure and administration of the city, which is divided into 66 wards.</p>
<p>Vivek Narayan Shejwalkar is the Mayor of Gwalior Municipal Corporation from the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gwalior Municipal Corporation covers an area of 47 square kilometres (18 sq mi) including the areas of Lashkar, Morar up to Deen Dayal Nagar (Gwalior Airport). The municipality was created on 6 June 1887 with two divisions for Lashkar and Morar, which later were merged with a single constitutional body.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_Government_Institutions">State Government Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: State Government Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li>Office of The Commissioner-Land Records &amp; Settlements Madhya-Pradesh</li>
<li>Office of The State Excise Commissioner of Madhya-Pradesh</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_connectivity">Transport and connectivity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport and connectivity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior is a major railway junction in the Northern central region. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwalior_Junction" title="Gwalior Junction">Gwalior Junction</a> (Station code: GWL) is the part of the <a href="/wiki/Jhansi_division" title="Jhansi division">Jhansi division</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Central_Railways" title="North Central Railways">North Central Railways</a>. Gwalior is one of the few places where both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narrow_gauge" title="Narrow gauge">narrow gauge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broad_gauge" title="Broad gauge">broad gauge</a> railways tracks are operational. Gwalior is the terminus for the longest narrow gauge route operating in the world, covering a distance of 198 km from Gwalior Junction to Sheopur. Gwalior Junction is a five railway track intersection point. It won an award for the best and cleanest station of <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Railway_zone" title="North Central Railway zone">North Central Railway zone</a>.</p>
<ol>
<li>Goes to <a href="/wiki/Agra_Cantonment_railway_station" title="Agra Cantonment railway station">Agra</a> (AGC)</li>
<li>Goes to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jhansi_Junction" title="Jhansi Junction">Jhansi</a> (JHS)</li>
<li>Goes to <a href="/wiki/Shivpuri_district" title="Shivpuri district">Shivpuri</a> (SVPI)</li>
<li>Goes to <a href="/wiki/Etawah_district" title="Etawah district">Etawah</a> (ETW)</li>
<li>Goes to <a href="/wiki/Sheopur_district" title="Sheopur district">Sheopur Kalan</a> (SOE) on Narrow Gauge Line</li>
</ol>
<p>Gwalior is one of the major commercial railway stations of the North Central Railway, whose zonal headquarters is centred in Allahabad. The station has won awards from Indian Railways for excellent clean infrastructure in 1987, 1988, 1989 and 1992. It is in the Adrash Station Category of Indian Railways. The government has decided to build escalators at this station, and the construction has started.</p>
<p>Gwalior narrow gauge railway connects to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kuno_National_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kuno National Park (page does not exist)">Kuno National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sheopur" title="Sheopur">Sheopur</a>. It is the junction point to reach tourist destinations like Shivpuri, Dholpur and Bhind. Gwalior is on the Main train line between <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> (station code: NDLS) and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> (Bombay) (CSTM) and between Delhi and <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> (MAS).</p>
<p>Some trains starting here and travelling towards Eastern India via Gwalior Junction – Jhansi Junction provide direct connections to points in Eastern India including <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> (Calcutta), <a href="/wiki/Barauni_Junction_railway_station" title="Barauni Junction railway station">Barauni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varanasi_Junction_railway_station" title="Varanasi Junction railway station">Varanasi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Allahabad" title="Allahabad">Allahabad</a>. There are about 50 trains to <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi_railway_station" title="New Delhi railway station">New Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> every day, and around the same number of trains to <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_Junction_railway_station" title="Bhopal Junction railway station">Bhopal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nagpur_Railway_Station" title="Nagpur Railway Station">Nagpur</a> stations. However, fewer trains are available for long routes like Mumbai and Chennai. The luxury trains – the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maharaja_Express" title="Maharaja Express">Maharaja Express</a> and the India on Wheels – stop at Gwalior on their week-long round trip of tourist destinations in Central India. More than 180 trains stop at Gwalior Railway Station <a class="external autonumber" href="http://indianrailways.info/stations/GWL/" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior is fairly well connected to other parts of Madhya Pradesh and India by national and state highways. The proposed <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_and_East%E2%80%93West_Corridor" title="North–South and East–West Corridor">North-south-Corridor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral" title="Golden Quadrilateral">Golden-Quadrilateral</a> Highway project passes through the city. The Agra-Bombay national highway (NH3) passes through Gwalior, connecting it to Shivpuri on one end and Agra on the other. The city is connected to the <a href="/wiki/Jhansi" title="Jhansi">Jhansi</a> by the National Highway 75, towards the south of the city. The northern part of the city is connected to the holy city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mathura,_Uttar_Pradesh" title="Mathura, Uttar Pradesh">Mathura</a> via National Highway 3. There are bus services to and from all major and minor cities near Gwalior, including <a href="/wiki/Bhopal" title="Bhopal">Bhopal</a>, Agra, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jabalpur" title="Jabalpur">Jabalpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jhansi" title="Jhansi">Jhansi</a>, Bhind, Morena, Dholpur, Etawah, Datia, <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indore" title="Indore">Indore</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior Airport (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>GWL</b>, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>VIGR</b>), also called Rajmata Vijya Raje Scindia Vimantal, is the airport of Gwalior. It has an Indian Air Force Base which stations Mirage fighters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Public_Transport">Local Public Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Local Public Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior's public transport system mainly consists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tempo_(car)" title="Tempo (car)">Tempos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaw taxis</a>, and micro-buses. Municipal Corporation's "Gwalior City Bus" covers some routes in the city. Blue <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">Radio taxis</a> are also available in Gwalior. The Tempos and auto rickshaws are often cited as a cause of pollution and road congestion, and the local government has plans to replace the Tempos with vans that will run on liquefied petroleum gas.<br/>
Recently, a 3 km cycle track has been built in the city, and the city became the fourth in India to have this type of facility.</p>
<p>The Gwalior Metro is the proposed project for Gwalior city. The project was announced by state CM Shivraj Singh Chouhan on October 17, 2014. Hence district administration is preparing a DPR(Detailed Project Report) for The Gwalior Metro.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art.2C_Literature">Art, Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Art, Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gwalior holds a major and a special position in the Indian classical music, art and literature. Gwalior is a well acknowledged place of art, associated with historic as well as contemporary evidence. In August 2005 a mural created by <a href="/wiki/Aasutosh_Panigrahi" title="Aasutosh Panigrahi">Aasutosh Panigrahi</a> and five other artists was acknowledged as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_Indoor_Mural" title="Largest Indoor Mural">World's Largest Indoor Mural</a> by <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marathi_Sahitya_Sammelan" title="Marathi Sahitya Sammelan">Marathi Sahitya Sammelan</a>, the conference on Marathi Literature was held in Gwalior in 1961. It was presided over by writer <a href="/wiki/Kusumavati_Deshpande" title="Kusumavati Deshpande">Kusumavati Deshpande</a> (herself a poet and also the wife of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavi_Anil" title="Kavi Anil">Kavi Anil</a>). She was the first female president of the annual Sammelan since its inception in 1878. Culturally Gwalior is the confluence of two rich cultures Bundeli and <a href="/wiki/Braj" title="Braj">Braj</a>.</p>
<p>In more recent times, Akhtar family has been based out of Gwalior for atleast 3 generations with <a href="/wiki/Muztar_Khairabadi" title="Muztar Khairabadi">Muztar Khairabadi</a>, his son <a href="/wiki/Jan_Nisar_Akhtar" title="Jan Nisar Akhtar">Jan Nisar Akhtar</a> and his grandson <a href="/wiki/Javed_Akhtar" title="Javed Akhtar">Javed Akhtar</a> being the prominent literary figures. <a href="/wiki/Nida_Fazli" title="Nida Fazli">Nida Fazli</a>, one of the most famous Indian Hindi and Urdu poets grew up here. Former Indian Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee" title="Atal Bihari Vajpayee">Atal Bihari Vajpayee</a>, is also a well known writer and poet.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raja Man Singh Tomar, the King of Gwalior between 1486 and 1516 AD, was a patron of <a href="/wiki/Dhrupad" title="Dhrupad">Drupad</a> (Hindi: ध्रुपद). Dhrupad is a vocal genre in Hindustani classical music, said to be the oldest still-in-use in that musical tradition. Its name is derived from the words "dhruva" (fixed) and "pada" (words). The term may denote both the verse form of the poetry and the style in which it is sung.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tomb_of_Tansen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="320" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Tomb_of_Tansen.jpg/220px-Tomb_of_Tansen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Tomb_of_Tansen.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tomb_of_Tansen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tomb of Tansen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gwalior holds a major position in the Indian classical music, with being the birthplace of the oldest Hindustani sangeet <a href="/wiki/Gharana" title="Gharana">gharana</a> - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwalior_Gharana" title="Gwalior Gharana">Gwalior Gharana</a>. Gwalior holds an unparalleled reputation in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangeet_(music)" title="Sangeet (music)">Sangeet</a> and has retained Indian traditions and the wealth of music intact over the years. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwalior_Gharana" title="Gwalior Gharana">Gwalior Gharana</a> is not only the oldest Khyal <a href="/wiki/Gharana" title="Gharana">Gharana</a> but it is also one of the most prominent <a href="/wiki/Gharana" title="Gharana">gharana</a> being the one to which most classical Indian musicians can trace the origin of their style. The rise of the Gwalior Gharana started with the reign of the great Mughal emperor Akbar (1542–1605). The favourite singers of this patron of the arts was <a href="/wiki/Tansen" title="Tansen">Tansen</a>. Tansen was first amongst the vocalists at the mughal court of Akbar and came from the town of Gwalior.</p>
<p>Tansen, born in Behat, trained in music at Vrindavan, served Raja Ramchandra Waghela of Bandhawgarh, then went to Agra under the patronage of <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>. An exponent of the Hindustani classical music's dhrupad style, he was counted among the Nine Jewels of the Royal Court. After the death of Tansen in Fatehpur Sikri and cremation in Agra, his ashes were buried in Gwalior. In remembrance of this artist there is a tomb constructed in Gwalior called the Tansen Tomb. <a href="/wiki/Tansen_Samaroh" title="Tansen Samaroh">Tansen Festival</a> started in the 1930s. At present, artists from all over the country come to perform in the festival.</p>
<p>Baijnath Prasad (alias <a href="/wiki/Baiju_Bawra" title="Baiju Bawra">Baiju Bawra</a>) was a classical singer (Dhrupadiya) who lived in Gwalior for his whole life under the patronage of Man Singh. Baiju was born in Chanderi and was cremated there. He received his musical training in Vrindaban under Swami Guru Haridas Ji. He was the court musician of Gwalior along with Nayak Charju, Bakshu, and others.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sarod" title="Sarod">Sarod</a> player <a href="/wiki/Amjad_Ali_Khan" title="Amjad Ali Khan">Amjad Ali Khan</a> is also from the city of Gwalior. His grandfather, Ghulam Ali Khan Bangash, became a court musician in Gwalior.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Tansen Music Festival</b>- The <a href="/wiki/Tansen_Samaroh" title="Tansen Samaroh">Tansen Sangeet Samaroh</a>, (Tansen Music Festival), is celebrated every year on the Tansen Tomb in Gwalior during the month of December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Tansen Samaroh is a platform where artists from all over India gather and participate to deliver vocal and instrumental performances. Gwalior's environment during the festival turns mystical with melodious music echoing. Music lovers from far and wide make it a point to be a part of this event at any cost, as it is a memorable experience for them. The Tansen Sangeet Samaroh is organised by the government of Madhya Pradesh, in association with the Academy of the Department of Culture. During the festival, music lovers and artists from all over the world gather to offer their tribute to Tansen. The academy offers honours to senior celebrities and junior artists by including them in the Samaroh through their music of performance.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sarod_Ghar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sarod Ghar (page does not exist)">Sarod Ghar</a> - This Museum of Music has been set up in the old ancestral house of musician <a href="/wiki/Hafiz_Ali_Khan" title="Hafiz Ali Khan">Hafiz Ali Khan</a>. It houses ancient instruments of the Indian masters of the past. It also houses an impressive collection of photographs and documents. Sarod Ghar is a unique institution devoted to promoting Indian classical music, heritage and culture. Through this 'window' to the past, music lovers can gain a better understanding of the evolution and history of our classical music and a deeper perspective and insight into the context of the art as it exists today.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communication">Media and communication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media and communication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are newspapers, magazines, local TV stations and four FM radio stations in Gwalior.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_Patrika" title="Rajasthan Patrika">Patrika</a></i> is the leading newspaper and <i><a href="/wiki/Dainik_Bhaskar" title="Dainik Bhaskar">Dainik Bhaskar</a></i> is one of the oldest and most widely read newspapers. <i>Swadesh</i> and <i>Naidunia</i> are other well-established newspapers. More newspapers published in Gwalior are <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BPN_Times&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BPN Times (page does not exist)">BPN Times</a></i>, <i>Raj Express,</i> <i>Dainik Madhya Raj</i>, <i>Nav Bharat</i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Youth_Engine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Youth Engine (page does not exist)">Youth Engine</a></i>, <i>Dainik Jagran, People's Samachar, Dainik Adityaz</i>. Evening newspapers are <i>Sandhya Samachaar, Gwalior Sandesh, Sudarshan Express</i>.</p>
<p>"Aalekh-Life in Pages" is one of the leading youth magazine published and widely read across the city. <i>SouLSteer</i> magazine is a bi-monthly lifestyle and automotive magazine in Gwalior.</p>
<p>The radio industry has expanded with private FM channels being introduced. The FM radio channels that broadcast in the city include <a href="/wiki/BIG_FM_92.7" title="BIG FM 92.7">Big FM</a> (92.7 MHz), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chaska_FM&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chaska FM (page does not exist)">Chaska FM</a> (95 MHz), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=My_FM_(94.3_MHz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="My FM (94.3 MHz) (page does not exist)">My FM (94.3 MHz)</a>, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lemon_(91.9_MHz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lemon (91.9 MHz) (page does not exist)">Lemon (91.9 MHz)</a>. The state-owned company, <a href="/wiki/Doordarshan" title="Doordarshan">Doordarshan</a>, transmits two terrestrial television channels. The city has local TV stations from companies. Major local channels include Hathway Win, Harsh Networks, KMJ Communications, and DEN networks.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lakshmibai National University for Physical Education (operational since 1957) is the largest physical education institutions in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Gwalior also has the Railway Hockey Stadium with artificial turf. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roop_Singh_Stadium" title="Roop Singh Stadium">Roop Singh Stadium</a> is a cricket ground with a capacity of 45,000. The stadium has hosted 10 One Day International (ODI) matches. Of the 10 matches played so far, the first one was played between India and West Indies on 22 January 1988. The ground has flood lights and has also hosted day-night encounters. One match of the 1996 Cricket World Cup was also played on this ground, between India and West Indies.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dhyan_Chand" title="Dhyan Chand">Dhyan Chand</a> was a famous hockey player from Gwalior. It was even told that he miraculously kept the ball stuck to his stick and was often referred to as a <i>Jaadugar</i><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> of Hockey. <a href="/wiki/Ankit_Sharma_(cricketer)" title="Ankit Sharma (cricketer)">Ankit Sharma</a> is a cricketer from Gwalior and playing in the Indian Premier League. Athletics is also played in this city, Vishal Kaim was the youngest hammer thrower of India when he participated in National Athletics Games in 2006 at the age of 14 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium_and_Sports_University">Stadium and Sports University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Stadium and Sports University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Captain_Roop_Singh_Stadium" title="Captain Roop Singh Stadium">Captain Roop Singh Stadium</a> is a cricket ground in Gwalior. The stadium has hosted 10 <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> (ODI) matches. Of the 10 matches played so far, the first one was played between India and West Indies on 22 January 1988. The ground has flood lights and has hosted day-night encounters. It can hold 45,000 people at a time. It was originally a hockey stadium named after great Indian hockey player <a href="/wiki/Roop_Singh" title="Roop Singh">Roop Singh</a>, brother of hockey player Dhyan Chand. The ground has flood lights and has hosted day-night encounters as well. One match of the 1996 Cricket World Cup was also played on this ground, between India and West Indies. This ground is notable for hosting the ODI between India and South Africa in which <a href="/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar" title="Sachin Tendulkar">Sachin Tendulkar</a> scored the first-ever double century in ODI cricket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lakshmibai_National_University_of_Physical_Education" title="Lakshmibai National University of Physical Education">Lakshmibai National University of Physical Education</a> (LNIPE), Gwalior was established by the Ministry of Education &amp; Culture, Government of India as Lakshmibai College of Physical Education (LCPE) in August 1957, the centenary year of the War of Independence. It is located at Gwalior, where Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi, a heroine of the war, died during the rebellion in 1857. The Institute started as an affiliated college of the Vikram University, Ujjain and then came to the folds of Jiwaji University, Gwalior in 1964. The Institute was given the status of National importance, and hence it was renamed as Lakshmibai National College of Physical Education (LNCPE) in1973. In recognition of its unique status and character and to facilitate its further growth, the college was conferred the status of an ′Autonomous College′ of Jiwaji University, Gwalior in 1982.</li>
<li>A new international stadium at Shankarpur village near Ghatigaon tehsil<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> has been proposed by <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh_Cricket_Association" title="Madhya Pradesh Cricket Association">Madhya Pradesh Cricket Association</a> (MPCA). The proposed stadium will be built on a land of 30 acres, which has been taken over by Gwalior District Cricket Association (GDCA). The construction of the proposed stadium is expected to be completed in 2017. It will have a seating capacity of around 100,000 spectators. It will also be equipped with flood lights for night matches, a swimming pool, sauna bath, modern gym, dressing room, and 30 corporate boxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IIITM_GH.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IIITM_GH.JPG/220px-IIITM_GH.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IIITM_GH.JPG/330px-IIITM_GH.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IIITM_GH.JPG/440px-IIITM_GH.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>

<p>In the last few years, Gwalior has developed into a significant centre of education. It hosts many prominent government as well as private universities and institutions including the following:</p>
