<p>Gwalior has five <a href="/wiki/Kendriya_Vidyalaya" title="Kendriya Vidyalaya">Kendriya Vidyalayas</a> (managed by the Ministry of Human Resource Development, Government Of India),several Engineering and Technological Institutes and more than 30 affiliated engineering colleges.</p>
<p>The famous Scindia School, boarding school for boys, and all India ranked 3rd among other IPSC Boarding schools by the Education World, Scindia Kanya Vidyalaya, boarding school for girls, are also located in Gwalior city.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_Fair.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gwalior_Fair.JPG/220px-Gwalior_Fair.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gwalior_Fair.JPG/330px-Gwalior_Fair.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gwalior_Fair.JPG/440px-Gwalior_Fair.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_Fair.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gwalior Fair</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gwalior is surrounded by 3 Industrial areas – Sitholi, Banmore and Malanpur. All three of these sectors are on NH 75, NH-3 and NH 92 respectively, with Malanpur being the largest. The city used to have big manufacturing industries, such as Gwalior Grasim and J.C. MILLS of Birlanagar, but now this sector is left with only one major factory – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.B.Mangharam" title="J.B.Mangharam">J.B.Mangharam</a> Ltd. But the other 3 sectors have many industries. The important ones are from dairy, chemical, manufacturing, textiles, and other industries. Handicraft and small industries are also found like Gwalior potteries. Gwalior is also an important historical and tourism sector of the country. Therefore, the tourism sector also puts an effect into the city's economy. Gwalior is part of NCR. The Gwalior Trade Fair is an annual trade fair showcasing the economy of Gwalior. There are some manufacturing set-ups of some companies like UFlex (Flex Industries Ltd), SRF, <b>Ranbaxy Laboratories</b>, <a href="/wiki/Cadbury" title="Cadbury">Cadbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._K._Organisation" title="J. K. Organisation">J. K. Tyres</a>, Surya Bulbs, SiyaRam and Railway spring factory Sitholi.' Most of the Local population is involved with trading firms or are self-employed. Many run OMEs and SMEs with Gwalior and Agra as the local market. The city is scattered with coaching institutes and Educational institutions which provide employment to a large section of city's population.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:240_Gwalior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/240_Gwalior.jpg/220px-240_Gwalior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/240_Gwalior.jpg/330px-240_Gwalior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/240_Gwalior.jpg/440px-240_Gwalior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:240_Gwalior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The town hall situated at Maharaj Bada</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_fair">Trade fair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Trade fair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Gwalior_trade_fair" title="Gwalior trade fair">Gwalior trade fair</a></b> was started in 1905 by Maharaja Madho Rao Scindia, King of Gwalior. It has become the biggest fair of Madhya Pradesh and one of the most colourful fairs of India. It starts in the second week of January and continues until February.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_markets">Major markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Major markets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Maharaj Bada is the biggest and most important market of Gwalior. Seven ancient buildings of different styles of architecture (Italian, Russian, Maratha, Mughal, Rajputi, Chinese, etc.) can be viewed.</li>
<li>Ghas Mandi- this area is presumed to be 700 years old it was established around the 15th century this place was used by local population for business by selling grass for feeding animals for king and other rich people.</li>
<li>Loha Mandi- this place is also 600 years old in Gwalior. this place was used for buying iron materials.</li>
<li>Hazira- it was the main market place of Gwalior that time. Nowadays this place is congested because of its irregular and unplanned structure made by old merchants in the 15th century.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DD_MALL.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/DD_MALL.JPG/220px-DD_MALL.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/DD_MALL.JPG/330px-DD_MALL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/DD_MALL.JPG/440px-DD_MALL.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DD_MALL.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
traffic outside Deen Dayal City mall</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Gwalior has three shopping malls, DD City Mall with <a href="/wiki/Fun_Cinemas" title="Fun Cinemas">Fun Cinemas</a> multiplex, Maya-Gitanjali Mall with Gold Digital Multiplex and the Central Mall. Salasar Mall City Centre, similarly to DD City Mall, also contains a multiplex. There are several gaming zones, three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discoth%C3%A8que" title="Discothèque">Discothèques</a> (DnD, Barcode, and Spectrum), and a water park in Gwalior. "Sun City Amusement Park" is a family entertainment centre in Gwalior. The DD City Mall is one of the biggest malls of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a>. A multi-storeyed structure, it houses shops and showrooms of many national and international brands and has a number of eateries, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Fun_Cinemas" title="Fun Cinemas">Fun Cinemas</a> multiplex. There are also some international and well known fast food restaurants like <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino's Pizza">Domino's Pizza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway (restaurant)</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> in DD City Mall. <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> is adjacent to DD Mall.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gwalior_Metro_and_suburbs">Gwalior Metro and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Gwalior Metro and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_town">Old town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Old town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The old town of Gwalior, commonly called Kila Gate is around 1 kilometre (0.62 mi) from Hazira, the largest area in old town, which is of considerable size but irregularly built. It lies at the eastern base of the rock and contains the tomb of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> saints, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Khwaja_Khanoon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Khwaja Khanoon (page does not exist)">Khwaja Khanoon</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ghaus" title="Muhammad Ghaus">Muhammad Ghaus</a>, erected during the early part of Mughal emperor <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>’s reign, and the tomb of <a href="/wiki/Tansen" title="Tansen">Mian Tansen</a>, a great singer and one of the 'Nine Jewels' of Akbar's court. A town called by his name <i>Ghauspura</i> situated near the tomb of Mohaommed Ghaus.reold town consisted of some streets and mohallas which are presumed to be 700 to 800 yrs old areas in gwalior which are still backward areas in gwalior due to improper management of new town. these old areas are as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li>Koteshwar Temple. This temple is a 700-year-old temple of Lord Shiva whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shivling" title="Shivling">shivling</a> was on Gwalior Fort, but when the Mughals conquered it they ordered the shivling thrown out. When the troops did that, the shivling was automatically established in a field below the fort without any harm. Muslim Gazi told the emperor not to harm the shivling. In the late 18th century Scindias built a temple for that shivling, now known as Koteshwar Mahadev.</li>
<li>Baba Kapoor- this place is 500 meters away from Ghas Mandi. This place was named Baba Kapoor because of saint Shah Abdul Gafoor.</li>
<li>Kashi Naresh ki gali- this a 600 yrs old residential street in Gwalior it was given name as Kashi Naresh ki gali because in the 14th century when the emperor of Kashi was defeated in war he was sent to exile by oppositions at that time Gwalior emperor and Kashi's emperor were good friends when Kashi's emperor told Gwalior's emperor whole story, emperor gave him an entire street for living at that time which is now known as Kashi Naresh ki Gali. their family even now resides there in Kashi Naresh ki gali in Rajaji Ka Bada. (Meanings: naresh = king = rajaji; gali = street in Hindi language; bada = big area.)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lashkar_Subcity"><a href="/wiki/Lashkar_Gwalior" title="Lashkar Gwalior">Lashkar Subcity</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Lashkar Subcity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:244_Gwalior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/244_Gwalior.jpg/220px-244_Gwalior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/244_Gwalior.jpg/330px-244_Gwalior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/244_Gwalior.jpg/440px-244_Gwalior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:244_Gwalior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jiwaji Chowk at Gwalior</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The name of Lashkar is a <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> word meaning 'army' or 'camp', as this was originally the camp, and later the permanent capital, of the Scindia dynasty of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwalior_state" title="Gwalior state">Gwalior state</a>. Lashkar was the capital of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Bharat" title="Madhya Bharat">Madhya Bharat</a> from 1950 to 1956.</p>
<p><i>Jayaji Chowk</i> is the central focus of Lashkar, with a large square, a former opera house, banks, tea, coffee and juice stands and a municipal market building. Thriving bazaars surround the chowk. Many jewellery shops are situated near <i>Jayaji Chowk</i>, also known as Maharaj Bada. A source of water for the city is Tighra Dam, built on the Saank river 20 km to the north. The Gajra Raja Medical College, founded in 1946 by the Maharaja Jiwaji Rao Scindia and the Maharani Vijayaraje Scindia, is situated in Lashkar on Palace Road, near Katora Taal, together with a group of many hospitals. Jai Vilas Palace, patterned on the French <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">palace of Versailles</a>, is located here.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morar_Subcity">Morar Subcity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Morar Subcity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morar_Gwalior" title="Morar Gwalior">Morar Gwalior</a> (Morar Subcity) formerly a separate town, lies 5 kilometres (3.1 mi) east of the old city. It was formerly a British military <a href="/wiki/Cantonment" title="Cantonment">cantonment</a>. Morar is generally considered a rural farming town. The area is known as the "green part" of Gwalior because much of the area is still rural.</p>
<p>Morar was the scene of the most serious uprising in Central India. On 1 June 1858, Jayajirao led his forces to Morar to fight a rebel army led by <a href="/wiki/Tatya_Tope" title="Tatya Tope">Tatya Tope</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rani_Lakshmibai" title="Rani Lakshmibai">Rani Lakshmibai</a> and Rao Sahib. This army had 7,000 infantry, 4,000 cavalry and 12 guns while he had only 1,500 cavalry, his bodyguard of 600 men and 8 guns. In this attack, the rebel cavalry took the guns and most of the Gwalior forces except the bodyguard went over to the rebels (some deserted). The Maharaja and the remainder fled without stopping until they reached the British garrison at Agra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> By 1900 it had become a centre for local trade and had an important training industry, with a population of 19,179 in 1901.</p>
<p>One of the sun temples of India is situated in Morar at Residency Road. This Sun Temple was built by the Aditya Birla Trust.</p>
<p>The cantonment area makes up a large area of Morar which contains official residences for the Indian Army. It has many canteens for Army personnel. Saint Paul's School and Pragati Vidyapeeth School are nearby. There is an air force base in the Pinto Park region.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thatipur">Thatipur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Thatipur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_Fort.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gwalior_Fort.jpg/220px-Gwalior_Fort.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gwalior_Fort.jpg/330px-Gwalior_Fort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gwalior_Fort.jpg/440px-Gwalior_Fort.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_Fort.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
view of Gwalior Fort from the Old city</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thatipur is said to have got its name from State Army Unit 34, which once resided there. Gandhi Road divides Thatipur into two areas. Morar at one end of the road and Balwant Nagar on the other.</p>
<p>Thatipur primarily consists of residential areas like Darpan Colony, Madhav Rao Scindhiya Enclave, the government blocks, Vivek Nagar, and Suresh Nagar. Places of note are the Dwarikadhish Mandir, Bhagwan colony, Tomar building, <b>Chauhan Pyaau</b> (The Chauhan family), Galla Kothar, Ramkrishna Aashram, Saraswati Nagar, Govindpuri, <a href="/wiki/Gayatri_Vihar" title="Gayatri Vihar">Gayatri Vihar</a>, Shakti Vihar, Shakuntalapuri, Dushyant Nagar, Shanti Vihar, and Mayur market along with Sai Baba Mandir in Shakti Vihar colony.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The prominent hospitals of Gwalior include <a href="/wiki/Gajara_Raja_Medical_College" title="Gajara Raja Medical College">Gajara Raja Medical College</a> and the associated J.A. Hospital, Kamla Raja Hospital, Sahara Hospital, Mascot Hospital, Birla Hospital, Cancer Hospital &amp; Research Institute and many private doctor clinics. The Cancer Hospital &amp; Research Institute is a nationally acclaimed medical centre in <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">Oncology</a>. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Charitable_hospital" title="Charitable hospital">charitable hospital</a> named SATCH (<i>Shri Anandpur Trust Charitable Hospital</i>) which provides free treatment. There is a government <a href="/wiki/Ayurveda" title="Ayurveda">Ayurvedic</a> college and a private <a href="/wiki/Homeopathy" title="Homeopathy">homoeopathic</a> college (Vasundhara Raje Homoeopathic Medical College) which is run by the Biochemic and Homoeopathic Association of Gwalior, also providing health care education and services.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_developments">Future developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Future developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The SADA Counter Magnet City, under the Indian urban development NCR plan, has been introduced to increase investment in education, industry and real estate. This is hoped to counteract the closing of manufacturers such as Hotline, Cimmco and Grasim Gwalior. The Gwalior Master PLAN launched by the local collector and municipal corporation initiates to improve the basic civic infrastructure of the city to meet the growing population of the city as well as to make the city beautiful for the tourists. Gwalior is the fourth largest city of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and it is the biggest city of North Madhya Pradesh.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gwalior_Fort">Gwalior Fort</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Gwalior Fort">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_Fort" title="Gwalior Fort">Gwalior Fort</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG/220px-Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG/330px-Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG/440px-Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwalior_fort_front_side_view.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gwalior fort front side view</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the heart of Gwalior is Gwalior Fort of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomara" title="Tomara">Tomara</a> Dynasty. This formidable structure was reputed to be one of the most structurally sound forts of India, having been improved by Raja <a href="/wiki/Man_Singh_Tomar" title="Man Singh Tomar">Man Singh Tomar</a> where a previous structure existed. It occupies an isolated rock outcrop. The hill is steepened to make it virtually unscalable and is surrounded by high walls which enclose buildings from several periods. The old town of Gwalior lies at the eastern base of the fortress. Lashkar, founded by Daulat Rao Scindia, formerly a separate town that originated as a military camp, lies to the south, and Morar, also a formerly separate town, lies to the east. Gwalior, Lashkar and Morar are part of the Gwalior Municipal Corporation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Fort, popularly called "the Gibraltar of India", overlooks the city. The Emperor <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a> reputedly described it as "the pearl in the necklace of the forts of Hind". This fort's architecture is unique. It displays a Chinese influence on Indian architecture, as Chinese dragons have been crafted at the hilt of the pillars. This influence was due to trade between China and India at the time of the fort's construction.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teli_ka_Mandir,_Gwalior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg/220px-Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg/330px-Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg/440px-Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teli_ka_Mandir,_Gwalior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
view of Gujri Mahal and nearby areas from Gwalior Fort</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the death of <a href="/wiki/Sher_Shah_Suri" title="Sher Shah Suri">Sher Shah Suri</a> in 1545, who was ruling North India at that time, his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islam_Shah" title="Islam Shah">Islam Shah</a> shifted his capital from Delhi to Gwalior and constructed 'Sher Shah Mandir' (or 'Sher Shah Fort') in his father's memory. Islam Shah operated from Gwalior until his death in 1553. Islam Shah had appointed the Hindu warrior '<a href="/wiki/Hemu" title="Hemu">Hemu</a>' or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hem_Chandra_Vikramaditya" title="Hem Chandra Vikramaditya">Hem Chandra Vikramaditya</a> as his Prime Minister in Sher Shah Fort for the first time, who later on became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hem_Chandra_Vikramaditya" title="Hem Chandra Vikramaditya">Hem Chandra Vikramaditya</a> king at Delhi and established 'Hindu Raj' in North India, by virtue of winning 22 battles continuously from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> and defeating <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>'s army in <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> and Delhi on 6 October 1556.</p>
<p>In the east of the city are two examples of early <a href="/wiki/Mughal_architecture" title="Mughal architecture">Mughal architecture</a>: the mausoleum of the 16th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> Saint Ghous Mohammed and the tomb of Mian Tansen, a great singer and one of the 'Nine Jewels' of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_Emperor" title="Mughal Emperor">Mughal Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>'s court. Right next to them is the Gujari Mahal, built by Tomar Rajput King Man Singh Tomar on demand of his consort Gujar princess "Mrignayani" (meaning "having eyes like deer").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Mughal Emperor Akbar is also known to have organised hunting parties near Gwalior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Close to the heart of the city is <a href="/wiki/Jai_Vilas_Mahal" title="Jai Vilas Mahal">Jai Vilas Palace</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scindia" title="Scindia">Scindia</a> dynasty, patterned on the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">palace of Versailles</a>. It combines Tuscan, Italian and Corinthian styles of architecture. Historically and architecturally, Gwalior is interesting first as an ancient seat of <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a> worship; second for its example of palace architecture of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> period between 1486 and 1516; and third as an historic fortress. Many historical places are found near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dabra" title="Dabra">Dabra</a>-<a href="/wiki/Bhitarwar" title="Bhitarwar">Bhitarwar</a> Road. Prior to the founding of Gwalior, the region was also known by its ancient name of <b>Gopasetra</b>. The great Apabhramsha poet Pandit <a href="/wiki/Raighu" title="Raighu">Raighu</a> lived in Gwalior. Gwalior had an institutional seat of the <a href="/wiki/Bhattaraka" title="Bhattaraka">Bhattarakas</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kashtha_Sangh" title="Kashtha Sangh">Kashtha Sangh</a> and later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mula_Sangh" title="Mula Sangh">Mula Sangh</a>.</p>
<p>According to history,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the original fort of Gwalior was founded by the <a href="/wiki/Bargujar" title="Bargujar">Bargujar</a> Kings during the 34th/35th century of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kali_yuga" title="Kali yuga">Kali yuga</a> as per puranas available with them. His palace is the most interesting example of early Hindu work of its class in India. Another palace of even greater extent was added to this in 1516. The <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> emperors, <a href="/wiki/Jahangir" title="Jahangir">Jahangir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shah_Jahan" title="Shah Jahan">Shah Jahan</a>, added palaces to these two, the whole making a group of edifices unequaled for picturesqueness and interest by anything of their class in central India. Among the apartments in the palace was the celebrated chamber, named the Baradari, supported on 12 columns, and 45 ft (15 m) square, with a stone roof, forming one of the most beautiful palace-halls in the world. It was, besides, singularly interesting from the expedients to which the Hindu architect was forced to resort to imitate the vaults of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>. Of the buildings, however, which so excited the admiration of the first Mughal emperor <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a>, probably little now remains.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:247_Gwalior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/247_Gwalior.jpg/220px-247_Gwalior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/247_Gwalior.jpg/330px-247_Gwalior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/247_Gwalior.jpg/440px-247_Gwalior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:247_Gwalior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rock cut images of the Tirthankaras.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gopachal_Parvat" title="Gopachal Parvat">Gopachal Parvat</a> is situated on the mountainous terrain at the slopes of Gwalior Fort. Gopachal Parvat contains unique statues of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jain" title="Jain">Jain</a> <a href="/wiki/Tirthankara" title="Tirthankara">Tirthankaras</a>. The idol of <b>Lord Parshvanath</b> seated on a lotus (carved out of a single stone) is the largest in the world, towering at 47 feet in height and 30 feet in breadth. There is a series of 26 Jain statues in a single line. Built between 1398 and 1536 by Tomar kings, these Jain <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tirthankar" title="Tirthankar">Tirthankar</a></i> statues are one of a kind in architecture and a treasure trove of old Indian heritage and culture. Gopachal Parvat is located approximately 2 km from the railway station and bus stand.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Phul-Bagh.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1009" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Phul-Bagh.jpg/220px-The_Phul-Bagh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Phul-Bagh.jpg/330px-The_Phul-Bagh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Phul-Bagh.jpg/440px-The_Phul-Bagh.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Phul-Bagh.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The view of scindia palace from the fort</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Municipality Museum, one of the more important museums of the city, is situated a little distance from Rani Lakshmibai's tomb.
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gwl_museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gwl_museum.jpg/220px-Gwl_museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gwl_museum.jpg/330px-Gwl_museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gwl_museum.jpg/440px-Gwl_museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gwl_museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gwalior Municipal Corporation's Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li>Vivsvaan Mandir (Sun Temple), A newly built temple dedicated to the Sun god, the Sun Temple is located near the <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_Residency" title="Gwalior Residency">residency</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gwalior#Morar" title="Gwalior">Morar</a>, Gwalior. It is a facsimile of the Sun temple of Konark, Orissa and now this sun temple is one among the significant pilgrimage centres in Gwalior. The temple is located in a serene ambiance and a well-maintained garden within the temple premises is very attractive. This holy temple draws the locals and tourists alike who gather here to render their prayers. It makes one astounded that a shrine of comparatively modern origin is held in such high regard, and became one among the most sought after pilgrimage centres in the city.</li>
<li>Modern 5D is Madhya Pradesh's first multi-dimensional theatre launched in the 2011 trade fair of Gwalior. It was built by Gwalior's leading enterprise Modern Techno Projects (P) Ltd. Modern 5D is recognised as India's first own multi-dimensional theatre.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shyam_Vatika" title="Shyam Vatika">Shyam Vatika</a> is a banquet hall which has the world's largest indoor mural, as recognised by <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>.</li>
<li>Within the fort are some marvels of medieval architecture. The 15th century <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gujari_Mahal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gujari Mahal (page does not exist)">Gujari Mahal</a> is a monument to the love of Raja Mansingh Tomar for his intrepid Gujar Queen, Mrignayani. The outer structure of Gujari Mahal has survived in an almost total state of preservation; the interior has been converted into an archaeological museum housing rare antiquities, some of them dating back to the 1st century A.D. Even though many of these have been defaced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iconoclastic" title="Iconoclastic">iconoclastic</a> Mughals, their perfection of form has survived the ravages of time. Particularly worth seeing is the statue of Shalbhanjika from Gyraspur, the tree goddess, the epitome of perfection in miniature. The statue is kept in the custody of the museum's curator, and can be seen on request.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sas-Bahu_Temple" title="Sas-Bahu Temple">Sas-Bahu Temple</a> - A 9th-century shrine, Sas-Bahu temple in the fort allures not only the devotees but also the tourists with its artistic value. Despite what its name may suggest, these temples are not dedicated to Sas (mother-in-law) and Bahu (daughter-in-law) but rather the short form of Shashtra Bahu, another name of Lord Vishnu. These temples situated adjacent to each other and the larger one is elaborately decorated with beautiful carvings and sculptures. The roof of the larger temple is adorned with a marvelous lotus carving which is very fascinating. These ancient temples display exceptional architectural brilliance and are a perfect destination for pious people.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teli_ka_Mandir,_Gwalior2341.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="300" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior2341.jpg/220px-Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior2341.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Teli_ka_Mandir%2C_Gwalior2341.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teli_ka_Mandir,_Gwalior2341.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Teli-ka-Mandir</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Teli Ka Mandir (Telangana Mandir) - A structure of about 100 feet, Teli Ka Mandir in Gwalior Fort distinguishes itself from the other compositions of its time because of its unique architecture. Though the roof of the temple holds a Dravidian look, the sculptures are typically North Indian. The temple bears a close resemblance to the temple of Prathihara Vishnu, and is filled with images of coiled serpents, passionate couples, river goddesses, and a flying <a href="/wiki/Garuda" title="Garuda">Garuda</a>. The temple architecture follows the Indo-Aryan and Nagara styles that exhibit superior artistic calibre. A marvelous temple, believed to be among the oldest constructions in the fort, gives an enchanting experience to the visitor. The Telikā Mandir, or 'oil-man's temple', owes its name to Teli, a term for an oil grinder or oil dealer. Many suggestions have been put forward to explain this name historically, but in fact the name is not old, the temple being used for processing oil before the British occupied the fort and used the building, albeit temporarily, as a coffee shop. The Telikā Mandir is the loftiest temple among all the buildings in Gwalior Fort with a height of about 30m. The temple consists of a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garba_griha" title="Garba griha">garba griha</a></i>, that is, sanctum proper for the deity, and an <i><a href="/wiki/Antarala" title="Antarala">antarala</a></i> to enter into the temple. It can be approached by a flight of steps provided on the eastern side. The most striking feature of the temple is the wagon-vaulted roof, a form used over rectangular shrines which normally accommodated a row of Mother Goddesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The goddesses from the interior vanished centuries ago and have not been traced, even in fragments. The exterior walls of the temple are richly decorated with sculptures, many of which are damaged; the niches, shaped like temples, are empty. The building carries a dedicatory inscription to the goddess in a niche on the southern side, but otherwise does not have any history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The architectural style, discussed by a number of architectural historians, points to a date in the late 8th Century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The building was erected just as the Gurjara Pratihāras were asserting their power over central India. The entrance gateway on the eastern side is a later addition of the British period, made by Major Keith in 1881. It was built as a way of saving various historic pillars and other pieces no longer in their original context.</li>
<li>Jain rock-cut sculptures - A striking part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jain" title="Jain">Jain</a> remains at Gwalior is a series of caves or rock-cut sculptures, excavated in the rock on all sides, and numbering nearly a hundred, great and small. Most of them are mere niches to hold statues, though some are cells that may have been originally intended for residences. According to inscriptions, they were all excavated within a short period of about thirty-three years, between 1441 and 1474.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> One of the colossal figures is 57 ft (17 m) high, taller than any other in northern India.</li>
<li>Gurudwara Datta Bandi Choodh- Gwalior Fort also has the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gurudwara" title="Gurudwara">Gurudwara</a>, built in the memory of the sixth <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guru_Har_Gobind" title="Guru Har Gobind">Guru Har Gobind</a>. This Gurudwara is particularly large and grand, built entirely of marble with coloured glass decorating the main building. Recital of the <a href="/wiki/Guru_Granth_Sahib" title="Guru Granth Sahib">Guru Granth Sahib</a> creates a peaceful and sacred atmosphere. Mughal kings used to visit Gwalior regularly. There is a Gurdwara that was converted to a mandir of "kalli devi" and process is on to take it back by Sikhs.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jai_Vilas_Mahal">Jai Vilas Mahal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Jai Vilas Mahal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jai_Vilas_Mahal" title="Jai Vilas Mahal">Jai Vilas Mahal</a></div>
<p>Also called Jai Vilas Palace, is the residential palace turned museum of the Maratha rulers of Gwalior - the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scindias" title="Scindias">Scindias</a>. It is in the heart of the city. The palace has notable collections of antiques and also some of the old time gadgets and collections that can't be easily seen. The museum is one of the largest in Madhya Pradesh and has the world's largest chandelier and the complex is a mixture of British as well as Hindu architecture. The palace was made in 1874 as an attempt to bring the palace of Versailles to Gwalior.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tombs_.26_Chatris_of_Historic_Importance">Tombs &amp; Chatris of Historic Importance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Tombs &amp; Chatris of Historic Importance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chatris_of_Scindias&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chatris of Scindias (page does not exist)">Chatris of Scindias</a> is situated close to the city near Achaleshwar temple and is the burial place for the Scindias who ruled the city for many years. Designated persons like Maharaja Madhavrao Scindia, Vijayaraje Scindia and His Highness Jivajirao Scindia were cremated here.</li>
<li>Tansen's tomb: Gwalior is the birthplace of the musician <a href="/wiki/Tansen" title="Tansen">Tansen</a>. He was one of the "Nine Gems of Akbar".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Gaus Mohammad's tomb: The tombs of Great Gaus Mohammad and Tansen are situated on the same territory.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="2000" height="72" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg/220px-Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg/330px-Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg/440px-Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mohammad_gaus_tomb.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaus Mohammad tomb</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Tomb of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rani_Lakshmibai" title="Rani Lakshmibai">Rani Lakshmibai</a>, a famous freedom fighter, at Phoolbag area. It is here where the she died in 1858 fighting against the British. It is also her burial place.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sun_Temple_Gwalior">Sun Temple Gwalior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sun Temple Gwalior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG/220px-Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG/330px-Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG/440px-Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sun_Temple_-_GWL_-_F3101_Wiki_Veethi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sun Temple</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A temple built by Birla group is dedicated to the Sun god, the Sun Temple is located near residency at Morar, Gwalior. It is a facsimile of the Sun temple of <a href="/wiki/Konark" title="Konark">Konark</a>, Odisha and now this sun temple is one among the significant pilgrimage centres in Gwalior. It is the place which gives best examples of peace and neatness in Gwalior. The temple is located in a serene ambience and a well-maintained garden within the temple premises is very attractive. This holy temple draws the locals and tourists alike who gather here to render their prayers. It makes one astounded that a shrine of comparatively modern origin holds such a highest regard, and became one among the most sought after pilgrimage centres in the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gwalior_Zoo_.28Gandhi_zoological_Park.29">Gwalior Zoo (Gandhi zoological Park)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Gwalior Zoo (Gandhi zoological Park)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This is one of the most lively and beautiful zoological parks of Madhya Pradesh. Its main attractions include Jamuna, 3 white tigers, serpents, golden pheasants, sambhar, hyena, bison, and others.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG/220px-Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG/330px-Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG/440px-Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sambhar_at_Gwalior_zoo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sambhar at Gandhi Zoological Park (Gwalior zoo)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tighra_Dam">Tighra Dam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Tighra Dam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tighra_dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tighra dam (page does not exist)">Tighra dam</a> is located on the outskirts of the city, Tighra is a nice place for an outing. The dam is now being used to store water from the Sank river and supply water to the whole of the city. There is boating as well as adventure sports' facilities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swarna_Rekha_river">Swarna Rekha river</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Swarna Rekha river">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Swarna Rekha river is a reconstructed part of the Swarna Rekha river which was dried during the British raj. A boat ride is taken from Padav in central Gwalior to Gwalior Zoo.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_Parks_and_Gardens">Historic Parks and Gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Historic Parks and Gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Lashkar part of Gwalior has many beautiful parks including the <i>Phool Bagh</i> or the garden of flowers build for the welcome of prince of Cambridge and the <b>Italian Garden</b> - the garden which was used by the Scindias as a place of relaxation, is build in Italian texture with a water pool surrounded by musical fountains. Ambedkar Park and Gandhi Park are the other prominent parks.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_interest">Places of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Places of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indian_Skimmer_(8582799716).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="708" data-file-width="1058" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg/220px-Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg/330px-Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg/440px-Indian_Skimmer_%288582799716%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Datia_Mahal.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Datia_Mahal.JPG/220px-Datia_Mahal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Datia_Mahal.JPG/330px-Datia_Mahal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Datia_Mahal.JPG/440px-Datia_Mahal.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<dl>
<dt>Kuno National Park</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kuno_National_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kuno National Park (page does not exist)">Kuno National Park</a></div>
<p>Kuno Wildlife Sanctuary or Palpur-Kuno Wildlife Sanctuary (between latitudes of 25°30'- 25°53'N &amp; longitude of 77°07'-77°26'E) lies in the Sheopur district of north western Madhya Pradesh, a state in central India. It is about 120 kilometres from Gwalior.</p>
<p>An area of 344.686 square kilometres was set aside as a Wildlife Sanctuary in 1981. Since then this has been elevated to the Kuno Wildlife Division with an additional area of 900 square kilometres as a buffer area around the Sanctuary. The park is home to many species of wild animals including wolves, monkeys, leopards and nilgai.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Madhav National Park</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Madhav_National_Park" title="Madhav National Park">Madhav National Park</a></div>
<p>Madhav National Park is situated in Shivpuri District of Gwalior region in northwest Madhya Pradesh, India. It is the ancestral home of the line of ęAli Khan, a region based in Punjab, and noted for the laws of commonly credited with defining modern day jurisprudence. Shivpuri town is located at 25°40' North, 77°44' East on Agra to Bombay National Highway-3. Shivpuri is steeped in the royal legacy of its past, when it was the summer capital of the Scindia rulers of Gwalior. Earlier its dense forests were the hunting grounds of the Mughal emperors. Emperor Akbar captured herds of elephants for his stables while returning from Mandu in year 1564. This National Park has a varied terrain of forested hills and flat grasslands around the lake. It is very rich in Biodiversity.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Padavali and Mitavali</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bateshwar,_Morena" title="Bateshwar, Morena">Bateshwar, Morena</a></div>
<p>Bateshwar (Hindi:बटेश्वर), 25 km from Morena town, is an archaeological site comprising about 200 ancient shrines in Morena district in Madhya Pradesh. This site is located on the north-western slope of a range of hills near Padavali, a village about 30 km from Gwalior. The shrines of Bateshwar temple-complex are dedicated mostly to Shiva and a few to Vishnu. The temples are made of sandstone and belong to the 8–10th century CE.[1] They were built during the reign of Gurjara-Pratihara Dynasty,[2] 300 years before Khajuraho temples were built.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Chambal River sanctuary</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chambal_River" title="Chambal River">Chambal River</a></div>
<p>The National Chambal Sanctuary lies between 24°55′ to 26°50′ N and 75°34′ to 79°18′E in Dholpur,60 km from Gwalior. It consists of the large arc described by the Chambal between Jawahar Sagar Dam in Rajasthan and the Chambal-Yamuna confluence in Uttar Pradesh. Over this arc, two stretches of the Chambal are protected as the National Chambal Sanctuary status - the upper sector, extending from Jawahar Sagar Dam to Kota Barrage, and the lower sector, extending from Keshoraipatan in Rajasthan to the Chambal-Yamuna confluence in Uttar Pradesh.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Sonagir</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sonagiri" title="Sonagiri">Sonagiri</a></div>
<p>Sonagiri (Hindi: सोनागिरी) about 60 km from Gwalior, has scores of Jain temples of 9th &amp; 10th century on little hills. This sacred place is popular among devotees &amp; ascetic saints to practice for self-discipline, austerity and to attain Nirvana since the time of Chandraprabhu (the 8th Teerthankar), five &amp; half crores of ascetic saints have achieved Moksa from here.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Datia</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Datia" title="Datia">Datia</a></div>
<p>Datia is the district headquarters of the Datia District in the north central Madhya Pradesh state of Central India. It is an ancient town, mentioned in the Mahabharata as Daityavakra. The town is 69 km from Gwalior, 325 km south of New Delhi and 320 km north of Bhopal. About 15 km from Datia is Sonagiri, a sacred Jain hill. Datia is also about 34 km from Jhansi, Uttar Pradesh and 52 km from Orchha. The nearest airport is at Gwalior. It was formerly the seat of the eponymous princely state in the British Raj.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Kanher Jhil</dt>
</dl>
<p>A popular picnic location near Ghatigaon, 25 kilometres (16 mi) from the city.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_individuals">Notable individuals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gwalior&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Notable individuals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

Tansen</div>
</div>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amjad_Ali_Khan" title="Amjad Ali Khan">Amjad Ali Khan</a>, sarod player and musician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee" title="Atal Bihari Vajpayee">Atal Bihari Vajpayee</a>, former Prime Minister of India</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Javed_Akhtar" title="Javed Akhtar">Javed Akhtar</a>, famous poet, lyricist &amp; writer, born in Gwalior. His family was based in Gwalior for nearly three generations, from his grandfather's time.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kartik_Tiwari" title="Kartik Tiwari">Kartik Tiwari</a>, actor, born in Gwalior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sharad_Kelkar" title="Sharad Kelkar">Sharad Kelkar</a>, actor, born in Gwalior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Piyush_Mishra" title="Piyush Mishra">Piyush Mishra</a>, Indian film and theatre actor, Music Director, Lyricist, Singer, Scriptwriter.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mamta_Sharma" title="Mamta Sharma">Mamta Sharma</a>, singer [Munni Badnam, Fevicol se etc.], born in Gwalior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ganesh_Shankar_Vidyarthi" title="Ganesh Shankar Vidyarthi">Ganesh Shankar Vidyarthi</a>, famous Hindi writer, born in Gwalior</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jyotiraditya_Scindia" title="Jyotiraditya Scindia">Jyotiraditya Scindia</a>, former Minister of Power</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Madhavrao_Scindia" title="Madhavrao Scindia">Madhavrao Scindia</a>, Indian politician and minister</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nida_Fazli" title="Nida Fazli">Nida Fazli</a>, famous Urdu writer and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roop_Singh" title="Roop Singh">Roop Singh</a>, Indian hockey player and Olympian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shivendra_Singh" title="Shivendra Singh">Shivendra Singh</a>, Indian national hockey player, born and lives in Gwalior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tansen" title="Tansen">Tansen</a>, court musician of the Mughal Ruler <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salman_Khan" title="Salman Khan">Salman Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arbaaz_Khan_(Indian_actor)" title="Arbaaz Khan (Indian actor)">Arbaaz Khan</a>, studied at Scindia School</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Narendra_Singh_Tomar" title="Narendra Singh Tomar">Narendra Singh Tomar</a>, Minister of Steel in Union Cabinet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pran_Kumar_Sharma" title="Pran Kumar Sharma">Pran Kumar Sharma</a>, cartoonist and comic creator of <a href="/wiki/Chacha_Chaudhary" title="Chacha Chaudhary">Chacha Chaudhary</a> fame moved here after the Partition</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunil_Bharti_Mittal" title="Sunil Bharti Mittal">Sunil Bharti Mittal</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Bharti Airtel</a>. He first joined the Wynberg Allen School in Mussoorie, but later attended Scindia School at Gwalior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anurag_Kashyap" title="Anurag Kashyap">Anurag Kashyap</a>, an Indian film director, screenwriter, producer and actor. He did his early schooling from Green School Dehradun and after the age of eight, he attended the Scindia School in Gwalior</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jivaji_Rao_Scindia" title="Jivaji Rao Scindia">Jivaji Rao Scindia</a>, last king of <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_State" title="Gwalior State">Gwalior State</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Krishnarao_Shankar_Pandit" title="Krishnarao Shankar Pandit">Krishnarao Shankar Pandit</a>, noted musician of the <a href="/wiki/Gwalior_gharana" title="Gwalior gharana">Gwalior gharana</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shri.S.D.Shrivastava&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shri.S.D.Shrivastava (page does not exist)">Shri.S.D.Shrivastava</a>, Kalakar Sab, Gold Medalist in Murels &amp; Fresco from JJ School of Arts, Mumbai. President of India awardee and Kalidas Samaan by Government of Madhya Pradesh.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Meet_Bros" title="Meet Bros">Meet Bros</a>, the musician duo hail from Gwalior.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pawan_Karan" title="Pawan Karan">Pawan karan</a>, Noted Indian major hindi poet and writer.</li>
</ul>
